sidewalk standards are specified in below a an alley shall be no longer than three hundred 300 feet without intersecting a local or collector road alleys shall not intersect arterial roads or highways b internal circulation roads provide offsite access to residential commercial office and similar units in larger land developments such as apartment complexes shopping centers and malls and office parks internal circulation roads link external roads to parking aisles or private garages c collector roads shall be designed as where practical to utilize their capacity and to reduce strain on intersecting collector and arterial roads and highways techniques to calm traffic and deter heavy trucks shall be utilized in residential areas d lane widths shall be the narrowest width feasible to serve the land development to calm traffic and reduce pedestrian crossing times the table provides wider lane widths for certain roads with medians twoway leftturn lanes or outside lanes to be shared with bicycle traffic e a landscaped median may be proposed in place of a twoway leftturn lane f typical curb radius standards are intended for roads designed for bicycle and pedestrian access and safety as well as slower vehicle speeds the planning commission may allow larger radii for existing roads with higher design speeds andor an unusually high percentage of heavy truck traffic  bike lanes dedicated bike lanes four 4 to six 6 feet wide shall be provided on all proposed roads designed with a target speed greater than thirty 30 miles per hour bike lanes may coincide with emergency lanes where applicable  onstreet parking a parking provided adjacent to the road whether or not within a road rightofway shall be designed to allow safe and efficient movement into and out of travel lanes parking stalls shall be spatially separated from lanes to provide visibility for motorists driving parking or disembarking parked vehicles this separation shall typically range from two 2 to ten 10 feet depending on the target speed and traffic volume of the road no such separation shall be required for parking aisles b no parking shall be designed to allow more than twenty 20 feet between the parking stall and the lane where motorists would back into the lane driveways to garages for singlefamily attached and detached homes shall be exempt c parallel parking onstreet parallel parking spaces should be twenty 20 to twentytwo 22 feet in length and seven 7 to nine 9 feet in width from face of curb d angled and perpendicular parking design standards for onstreet angled and perpendicular parking shall be identical to those for onsite parking below  tree planting along roadways a street trees the developer shall install street trees along arterial commercial collector and internal circulation roads in a major land development to calm traffic buffer private property from light and noise of traffic shade the road and sidewalks and reduce urban heat island effect if a road is maintained or is proposed to be maintained by a government entity that prohibits street trees roadside trees shall be required 1 one 1 street tree shall be installed per forty 40 feet of road on average measured at edge of pavement on each side of the road exclusive of intersections with other roads oncenter spacing between street trees shall be thirty 30 to fifty 50 feet 2 if curb bulbouts are proposed to define onstreet parking one 1 street tree may be planted in the bulbout in place of two 2 street trees otherwise required per a1 above 3 street trees shall be upright growing hardwood trees with an average life expectancy of at least forty 40 years 4 street trees shall be installed at three 3 inches in caliper in tree wells or in a verge between the road and the sidewalk 5 street trees shall be planted within the road rightofway or easement and protected from vehicular traffic by curbs swales or preexisting ditches a street trees shall be planted at least two 2 feet from barrier standing curbs b street trees shall be planted at least five 5 feet from rolled curbs 6 conservation of an existing tree three 3 inches or more in caliper in the road rightofway or easement may meet the requirement for a street tree b roadside trees the developer shall install roadside trees along local residential collector and industrial collector roads as well as highways in a major land development to calm traffic buffer private property from light and noise of traffic shade the road and sidewalks and reduce urban heat island effect 1 one 1 roadside tree shall be planted per fifty 50 feet of road rightofway on average measured at the edge of rightofway on each side of the road oncenter spacing between roadside trees shall be between twentyfive 25 and one hundred 100 feet 2 roadside trees may be planted in the road rightofway or easement or in the required front yard of adjoining lots 3 roadside trees shall be upright growing hardwood trees at least three 3 inches in caliper with an average life expectancy of at least forty 40 years 4 at least every third roadside tree shall be a canopy tree maturing to at least forty 40 feet in height the remainder may be understorey trees 5 an existing tree protected by hanahan zoning standards within twentyfive 25 feet of the road rightofway shall meet the requirement for one 1 roadside tree  road names a the developer shall submit road names for planning commission approval typically within final plat review the developer shall verify acceptability of the road names with berkeley county e911 prior to submitting them for hanahan planning commission review and approval b to prevent any confusion for emergency response vehicles names for proposed roads shall be sufficiently audibly different from all other roads in the following postal zip codes which cover hanahan as well as any future zip code area subdivided therefrom 294 294 and 29445 c road labels such as place street drive avenue and boulevard shall be applied to accurately represent the road eg a twolane local road shall not be labeled a boulevard and a fourlane divided facility shall not be labeled a place d a road proposed to intersect a crossroad immediately opposite an existing road shall carry the same name e a proposed road crossing a more significant road eg a local road crossing a collector shall be labeled east and west or north and south according to the general compass orientation of the proposed road 57  design and improvements standards for pedestrian facilities  general standards a proposed walkways shall provide at least six 6 feet lateral clearance from finished grade to seven 7 feet above finished grade the clear distance shall be at least one 1 foot wider than the width of the walkway and shall not extend into travel lanes of adjacent roadways b proposed walkways shall be at least four 4 feet wide c proposed walkways shall be significantly differentiated from their surroundings by color texture materials grade elevation or any combination thereof unless specifically stated otherwise to prevent ponding in the walkway and to protect users from automobile traffic d proposed walkways shall be constructed so as to prevent the erosion or deterioration of edges to withstand wear and tear from expected users and adverse natural conditions and events and to otherwise ensure their durability and longevity  sidewalks a on roads with target speeds thirty 30 miles per hour or greater sidewalks shall be separated from lanes on roads by at least five 5 feet except as needed to access crosswalks the interstitial space may be hardscaped or provided with vegetative ground cover b on roads with target speeds forty 40 miles per hour or greater sidewalks shall be separated from lanes on roads by at least ten 10 feet except as needed to access crosswalks the interstitial space may be hardscaped or provided with vegetative ground cover c on singleloaded local roads sidewalks shall only be required on the side of the street with proposed home sites but shall be at least six 6 feet wide d on permanent singleterminus local roads sidewalks shall only be required on one side of the street but shall be at least six 6 feet wide e proposed sidewalks shall meet or exceed standards of the americans with disabilities act as amended including curb ramps and passing areas as applicable f sidewalks shall be constructed of concrete bricks granite pavers or similar hardscape on a compacted base sufficient to support the surface and reasonably expected pedestrian traffic and outdoor furniture under all weather conditions g proposed sidewalks shall be constructed to withstand automobile traffic entering driveways or parking alongside the road where they are not reasonably protected from such  bikeped facilities a facilities designed for bicycle andor pedestrian circulation independent of a road ie not a sidewalk may be constructed with asphalt or permeable or natural surfaces like gravel such facilities shall be designed to ensure minimal loss of loose material over time eg edging and constructed on ground or base that adequately supports the surface material in all weather conditions while meeting the demands of expected traffic b internal blocks longer than eight hundred 800 feet shall be approximately bisected by midblock walkways to ensure adequate pedestrian access throughout the neighborhoods except where such walkways would end in wetlands or other inaccessible features c multiuse facilities proposed for bicycle and pedestrian traffic shall be at least eight 8 feet wide proposed twoway multiuse facilities should be at least ten 10 feet wide which the planning commission shall require for safety and access at any point the walkway enters a road rightofway or easement the width of the multiuse walkway may taper thereafter although this is discouraged  crosswalks a crosswalks shall connect all opposing curb ramps at intersections of proposed residential and commercial collector roads arterial roads commercial internal circulation roads and highways all crosswalks shall be provided with signs indicating the presence of the crosswalk in accordance with minimum scdot standards b crosswalks on residential collector roads and commercial internal circulation roads shall be comprised at a minimum of two fourinch white lines meeting scdot raised pavement marking standards the lateral distance between the lines shall be the same as the width of the sidewalks connected c other required crosswalks shall be articulated more significantly as acceptable to the planning commission and shall be linked with a pedestrian crossing signal at a traffic light or with flashing yellow lights that precede the crosswalk in both directions of vehicular traffic in accordance with scdot standards  courtyards a proposed courtyard shall be a park space on which proposed residential lots front and are oriented toward wet and dry ponds stormwater detention and retention facilities may be incorporated into the court as design elements a the courtyard shall include walkways that meet or exceed standards for local roads b the courtyard shall include street trees that meet or exceed standards for commercial collector roads c the courtyard shall be at least twentyfive 25 feet wide d the courtyard shall abut and be open to local roads with onstreet parking on at least fifteen 15 percent of its perimeter measured at edge of pavement and the footprints of abutting homes e vehicular access shall be provided to the rear of homes located on courtyards via twoway alleys or local roads that are hardscaped and designed and engineered to accommodate service vehicles fire truck garbage truck school bus etc  plazas a proposed plaza shall be a park space on which proposed commercial storefronts or office units front and are oriented toward the plaza shall typically include street furniture and articulated public spaces including but not limited to some combination of benches water features gazebos stages planter boxes and galleries a the plaza shall include walkways and street trees that meet or exceed standards for commercial collector roads b the plaza shall be at least forty 40 feet wide and no larger than onehalf 12 acre in size measured to heated walls of storefronts and curbs of adjoining streets c vehicular access shall be provided to the rear of stores and offices located on plazas via twoway alleys or local roads that are hardscaped and designed to accommodate service vehicles fire truck garbage truck school bus etc d plazas shall be designed to prevent regular vehicle traffic but shall accommodate aerial fire trucks so that potential fires can be fought by firefighters e the plaza shall abut and be open to commercial collector roads with onstreet parking on at least fifteen 15 percent of its perimeter measured from edge of pavement and the footprints of abutting homes breakaway bollards are recommended at the opening to deter motorists but to allow access by emergency response vehicles 58  sanitation service a curbside pickup land developments proposed for curbside trash pickup shall be designed so as to minimize backtracking by sanitation vehicles by limiting singleterminus streets and providing two 2 routes of egress from each lot to the exterior of the land development as practical b community pickup land developments proposed for community trash pickup shall locate the dumpsters at convenient points of access for users and sanitation vehicles to the extent practical dumpsters shall be located along alleys or internal circulation roads that can be easily accessed by sanitation vehicles but that are not easily visible from public view where practical dumpsters shall be located to the rear and not near the public face of structures screening and buffering per landscaping standards of the hanahan zoning shall apply 59  parking  general standards a all proposed parking areas shall be designed as part of a unified circulation plan that safely and efficiently provides access to each lot land use residence office shop or similar unit exclusive of natural constraints parking areas for separate parcels and land uses in a proposed land development shall be accessible to one 1 another so as to allow motorists to pass from one 1 parking area into another without reentering collector or arterial roads or highways b all proposed parking areas shall be designed so that sanitation emergency and other public service vehicles can safely and efficiently serve the development for which parking is proposed c circulation areas shall be designed so that vehicles can proceed safely without posing a danger to pedestrians or parked vehicles d parking areas shall be constructed of durable allweather surfaces resistant to ponding adequate to accommodate regular use by vehicles routinely generated by the proposed development e separate egress point shall be considered one 1 access point 2 a parcel with two hundred 200 feet or more of frontage shall provide no more than two 2 access points onto the roads for the purpose of this provision an ingress point and a separate egress point shall be considered one 1 access point 3 multiple parcels in a proposed land development shall be provided with shared access points where of the hanahan zoning g loading zones the developer of a nonresidential land development shall make a parking space available to the development as needed by the proposed land use 1 each space shall section 2 all land development proposals shall provide vehicular access to the parcel which shall be accomplished via private access or community access and parking area 3 driveways shall be designed curb or pavement edge 510  illumination of vehicular and pedestrian facilities a the developer shall propose a system of illumination of all roads and adjacent sidewalks within a major land development illumination shall provide lighting for the safety of the traveling public without causing nuisances to adjoining land uses due to glare or intensity the proposal shall meet or exceed the american national standard practice for roadway lighting illuminating engineering society of north america 200 as amended b illumination of vehicular and pedestrian facilities in all proposed land developments shall be provided by fixtures appropriate to the facility and surrounding land uses in size height scale and oncenter spacing 511  stormwater and floodplain management  general standards for erosion and sediment reduction and stormwater management a the developer shall propose a stormwater management system that prevents damage to structures and land within the proposed land development that prevents increases in stormwater runoff onto property downstream of the proposed development and that prevents additional stormwater accumulation upstream of the proposed development moreover the developer shall propose a stormwater management plan that minimizes water pollution discharges from the proposed land development to the extent practical b the land development shall be designed to the extent practical to minimize grading filling and alteration of land that disrupts natural drainage patterns c to the extent practical structures shall not be located such that natural or artificial drainage patterns and facilities would be impeded in a manner detrimental to surrounding properties within or adjacent to the proposed land development in addition property boundaries shall not be platted such that future structures would impede drainage in the same manner d the proposed land development shall tie into the existing stormwater drainage system where available and shall ensure that the volume and pollution level of water drained do not adversely impact the drainage system or the receiving water body to which the system discharges e primary drainage may be handled in the road system or to the interior of blocks bioretention swales are preferred conduits for runoff where drainage is handled to the interior of blocks drainage ditches are discouraged but may be used where advantageous for natural resource protection f measures to promote filtration percolation and plant absorption of site runoff are preferred to minimize demand for centralized wet ponds  stormwater management features in addition to bioretention swales and ditches acceptable stormwater management devices include bioretention cells retention and detention ponds stormwater sewer pipes and box culverts roadside gutters valley gutters and gutters with standing or mountable curbs perforated pipes trench drains and related inlet and discharge facilities common features appear below the planning commission may approve other features a bioretention features should be designed for twoyeartwentyfourhour storm events bioretention features should incorporate existing natural vegetation where practical b ponds ditches and swales should be cleared grubbed and graded to function properly maintenance shelves shall be cleared of underbrush but protected trees shall remain where practical c stormwater management features shall be protected as necessary from erosion with vegetation riprap or other stabilizing material d pond banks shall be protected from erosion with vegetation or other stabilizing material which shall at a minimum be sod or hydroseed littoral vegetation to filter nonpointsource pollution is preferred for the banks of wet ponds dry ponds shall be vegetated with sod or hydroseed at a minimum e land surrounding stormwater sewer pipes shall be cleared of underbrush but protected trees shall remain and pipes shall be installed to minimize disturbance of tree root systems within required tree protection areas f ditches and bioretention swales shall have a maximum side slope of  three 3 feet of run per foot of rise and a minimum flatbottom width of two 2 feet g the bottoms of swales and ditches shall be at least one 1 foot above the water table to prevent stagnant water collection and allow for percolation  application of berkeley county standards a where practical the proposed land development shall meet or exceed the requirements of the berkeley county stormwater drainage as amended and the berkeley county engineering construction and development standards manual b the developer may choose to deviate from berkeley county requirements with good cause as determined by the planning commission and in accordance with recognized professional engineering practices the developer shall then propose alternative means of stormwater management and indicate to the planning commission how these means meet the intent of this ordinance match or further reduce the risk of inundation from stormwater and match or further reduce water pollution resulting from inundation and stormwater runoff including erosion and sedimentation  application of state standards a where required by the south carolina codes and regulations the developer shall propose a plan that minimizes erosion and sedimentation during construction the plan and its implementation shall meet or exceed the standards of the south carolina office of ocean and coastal resources management ocrm which has jurisdiction the approved plans and letter denoting approval from ocrm shall be submitted to the city planner as part of an application for a land disturbance permit b where applicable the developer shall meet or exceed ocrm standards for stormwater management which typically require that the proposed development provide for stormwater management that neither increases nor decreases existing stormwater runoff the approved stormwater management plans and letter denoting approval from ocrm shall be submitted to the city planner as part of an application for a land disturbance permit  floodplain management standards a the developer shall account for flood hazard areas that occur on the land proposed for development it shall be the responsibility of the developer to locate boundaries of any floodplains delineated by the federal emergency management agency fema on the land and to indicate and label them in illustrations submitted during the land development review process b the proposed land development shall meet or exceed the standards of hanahan city  floodplain damage prevention c where practical development shall be concentrated on land out of floodplains type a planned developments shall locate required open space in floodplains where practical to minimize intrusion type b planned developments shall be encouraged to achieve the same and to indicate so in its proposed master plan and text regulating development within the planned development district d road standard related to flooding the centerline elevation of proposed roads shall be above the tenyear floodplain the planning commission may however modify this standard where necessary to prevent the filling of land resulting in loss of protected trees 512  water quality protection  state and federal standards for wetlands protection and mitigation a the developer shall survey land proposed for development and delineate wetlands where required by standards of sc office of ocean and coastal resources management andor us army corps of engineers delineated wetlands shall be indicated on the appropriate development plan submitted to the city of hanahan for review b the developer shall indicate all measures required by sc ocrm and us ace to protect wetlands or mitigate impacts thereto on the same development plan  wetlands protection standards a where practical the developer shall incorporate wetlands and any required wetland buffering whether by local or state standards into commonly owned property and not into numerous individually owned lots b maintenance shall be provided per deed restrictions restricting the disturbance and encroachment of wetlands and associated buffers shall be stated on each plat of a parcel containing these features c rear yard setbacks shall be measured from the highland edge of the wetland buffer where provided to prevent encroachment by construction activity  goose creek reservoir protection a a major land development shall designate all land within thirtyfive 35 feet of the ocrmrecognized critical line of the goose creek reservoir as a wetland buffer to protect the water quality of the reservoir state standards may require a deeper buffer the buffer shall be indicated on the preliminary land development plan b site redevelopment next to the reservoir for a major land development proposed on an existing developed site cleared of vegetation the proposed preliminary land development plan for redevelopment or expansion of the existing development shall propose planting the buffer 1 the planted buffer shall consist of six 6 canopy trees and thirtyfive 35 shrubs per one hundred 100 linear feet and natural groundcover to inhibit erosion slow sheet runoff and encourage permeation of runoff into the ground 2 the planning commission may modify this standard where it deems necessary to ensure quality redevelopment that furthers the objectives of this ordinance modernizes stormwater management remedies site contamination and takes alternative steps to mitigate water pollution  buffer design standards a preexisting natural vegetation in buffers required by the city of hanahan shall be preserved these areas promote filtration of stormwater runoff which inhibits nonpointsource water pollution entering the goose creek reservoir or other protected wetland b disturbances shall be limited to routine maintenance to remove noxious weeds invasive species and litter to prune trees and undergrowth and to plant supplemental vegetation if desired to improve the buffer aesthetically or functionally c encroachments into the buffer shall be limited to approved view corridors which may access docks and infrastructure that crosses the buffer and wetland as approved by applicable county state and federal authorities as well as the city of hanahan d view corridors up to twenty 20 feet wide may be cut buffer to afford views of wetlands the corridor shall be cut on an angle of at least thirty 30 degrees relative to the general orientation of the critical line across the parcel to prevent channeling of stormwater runoff in the corridor the cleared area shall be stabilized with grass mulch or other vegetative materials to prevent erosion and sedimentation of the wetland docks where approved by applicable state and federal authorities may be installed in the view corridor e trees throughout the buffer may be limbed up but no higher than onethird  13  of the height of the tree the removal of lower limbs affords property owners views of the wetland between the trees shrubs and other lowlying vegetation may be pruned down to four 4 feet provided no more than onethird  13  of each shrub is removed to allow views as well  buffer design standards for recreational access buffers fifty 50 feet or more in depth provided voluntarily may be encroached by pervious walkways a clearing and grubbing of vegetation and grading for the walkway shall be limited to the width of the walkway plus three 3 feet on both sides for shoulders twenty 20 feet shall be the maximum allowable width cleared and graded for the walkway b the shoulders of the walkway shall be revegetated mulched or otherwise stabilized to prevent erosion c the walkway shall be a pervious surface including but not limited to a boardwalk with spaced boards which may be raised for brief wetland crossings where approved by appropriate state and federal authorities 513  green space  open space unencumbered buildable land prior to proposed land development that is required for or otherwise committed to stormwater management nonjurisdictional wetlands wetland buffering natural and cultural resource conservation and landscaped common areas shall be considered open space for purposes of this ordinance and the hanahan zoning which may encourage or require open space conservation for land development approval wetlands required to be preserved by other entities including tidal marsh and the goose creek reservoir shall not be considered open space for these purposes land occupied by structures and vehicle circulation and parking is not open space  park space unencumbered buildable land prior to proposed land development that is programmed for passive or active recreation and leisure shall be considered park space for the purposes of this ordinance and the hanahan zoning which may encourage or require provision of park space for land development approval a park space shall include at a minimum one 1 of the following two 2 elements 1 a welldefined trail system for pedestrian access throughout the area indicated as park space which may include dense vegetation or an open field  or 2 an easily accessible open lawn passable by pedestrians throughout the lawn may include shade trees ornamental plantings flowerbeds park furniture public art and other outdoor amenities b park space shall include a program for regular maintenance including mowing pruning weeding mulching repaving replanting and irrigation as needed to maintain the intended appearance and accessibility c recreational wetland buffers standards for which appear above subsection  shall be considered park space other wetlands buffers shall be considered open space d wet and dry stormwater management ponds shall be considered park space when they are incorporated into a pedestrian circulation system and utilized as an aesthetic design feature ponds located to the rear of structures shall typically be considered open space e wetlands including tidal marsh and the goose creek reservoir shall not be considered park space for the purpose of land development review f for the purposes of the hanahan zoning and land development ordinances park space is neither occupied by fully enclosed structures nor programmed for vehicle circulation and parking  however adequate parking and facilities such as restrooms may be required or encouraged 514  potable water a access to potable water the developer shall demonstrate that each buildable lot within the proposed land development shall be provided access to potable water the means of potable water provision shall meet or exceed the standards of the south carolina department of health and environmental control and the water service provider where applicable from which service is desired 1 the developer proposing a land development within five hundred 500 feet of a public water system shall extend the water system to the land development if acceptable to the public water service provider the developer shall then extend the public water supply system to each buildable lot in the land development 2 onsite water supply the developer not required to extend public water system to a proposed land development may choose onsite water supply this developer shall demonstrate that each proposed buildable lot can be served by a private onsite system the developer shall make that system available prior to transferring the lot or shall make the installation of the system prior to issuance of a building permit a condition of sale for each lot this condition shall be noted on the deed to the property transferred b access to water for fire protection the developer proposing extension of the public water supply system shall install fire hydrants as required by building and fire codes as adopted by the city of hanahan 515  sanitary sewerage a ability to dispose of sewerage the developer shall demonstrate that each buildable lot within the proposed land development shall be provided direct access to sanitary sewerage along the road frontage of the parcel or have the capacity  including soils and environmental conditions  required for an onsite disposal system the means of sewage disposal shall meet or exceed the standards of the south carolina department of health and environmental control and the sanitary sewer service provider where applicable from which service is desired 1 the developer shall connect to sanitary sewerage as required by the berkeleycharlestondorchester council of governments under its regional water quality management plan 2 where proposed to serve the land development the sanitary sewer system shall be extended to each buildable lot in the proposed land development the extension shall meet or exceed the standards of the service provider for inclusion in the sanitary sewer system as public infrastructure 3 where connection to sanitary sewerage is not required or desired the developer shall demonstrate that each buildable lot has the capacity to accommodate an onsite disposal system b property redevelopment a parcel proposed for development with an existing onsite disposal system shall demonstrate where the redevelopment triggers compliance with this ordinance that the system is functioning properly routine maintenance shall be performed on the system prior to the issuance of a zoning permit for the property served in the event that the system is found deficient the applicant for a zoning permit shall rectify the condition by repairing or replacing the system or connecting to a sanitary sewer system c pump station where needed to adequately serve the land development as determined by the service provider the developer may include a pump station on a remnant parcel of land adjacent to a transportation rightofway or ingressegress easement the pump station shall be readily accessible to utility staff but shall be located to the extent practical in an unobtrusive location away from areas of potentially heavy pedestrian traffic and away from the primary entrances of nonresidential structures open to the public 516  other utilities a electrical power the developer shall demonstrate that each buildable lot within the proposed land development shall be provided access to electricity via written notice from the proposed provider that describes means of access and point of entry into the existing system the means of electrical power provision shall meet or exceed the standards of the proposed service provider b natural gas telephone television and internet access the developer who proposes natural gas telephone television and internet access via pipeline wire and cable as applicable shall meet or exceed the requirements of the service provider c utility lines 1 all utility lines proposed in a major land development shall be located underground and parallel to roads except as necessary to cross bridges connect to existing aboveground lines and connect structures served the lines and related equipment shall be readily accessible to utility staff 2 utility lines shall be collected in easements or rightsofway to the extent practical to use land more efficiently and to minimize disruption to and loss of natural vegetation d utility equipment location equipment related to the transmission of the utility shall be located in discreet locations to the extent practical such as lot corners the developer shall ensure that equipment is in no danger of inundation from stormwater and shall not locate equipment in or too near drainage facilities e major transmission the standards of this section are intended for the developer installing service within a proposed land development major transmission lines and related equipment may be designed and constructed to meet the needs of the utility provider the proposal shall not violate the objectives of this ordinance 517  rightsofway and easements  general standards a all public improvements shall be incorporated into an easement or rightofway dedicated to perpetual public use and assigned to an entity responsible for its maintenance per this shall be noted on the final plat and any record drawing illustrating public improvements b easements and rightsofway shall be of such dimensions to incorporate the public improvements including shoulders and banks and to provide sufficient access for adequate maintenance of the improvements  roads and driveways a all improvements intended for the traveling public shall be incorporated into a transportation rightofway dedicated to sc department of transportation berkeley county or a property owners association representative of all properties reliant upon the improvements for access established for the purposes of owning and maintaining the improvements exceptions shall be as follows 1 land intended for the expansion of a preexisting road and rightofway shall be reserved as an easement dedicated for that purpose land intended for the future extension of an existing or proposed road and rightofway shall be reserved as an easement dedicated for that purpose once constructed the improvements may be dedicated and incorporated into a transportation rightofway 2 two 2 neighboring lots with one 1 primary structure each may share a driveway within an ingressegress easement the easement shall be centered along the common lot line with a width equal to the width of the driveway and any provided sidewalks plus two 2 feet minimum on both sides 3 internal circulation roads in attachedunit residential community shall be incorporated into easements dedicated for perpetual access to the traveling public except where rightsofway are provided a property owners association representative of all properties reliant upon the improvements for access shall be charged with responsibility for maintenance of these internal circulation roads the easements shall occur on land owned by the same 4 access management the planning commission may encourage or the sc department of transportation or berkeley county may require the developer of a large land development to implement access management the purpose is to coordinate the access to the public rightofway from multiple parcels in a land development to reduce vehicular conflict points in the rightofway a to accomplish access management internal circulation roads in land developments shall be incorporated into easements dedicated for perpetual access to the traveling public except where rightsofway are provided the improvements in the easement shall be maintained by the largest landowner relying on access such as the anchor of a commercial land development or by a property owners association representative of all properties reliant upon the improvements for access b each parcel with frontage on the public rightofway shall nevertheless provide pedestrian access directly to and along that rightofway b no property shall be proposed to be solely reliant on an ingressegress easement for access except as provided for access management c an ingressegress easement incorporating a road shall not encroach a required yard setbacks required by zoning district shall be measured from the boundaries of the ingressegress easement  pedestrian facilities a sidewalks shall be incorporated into adjacent road rightofway where practical b other walkways may be incorporated into easements or rightsofway clear provisions for ownership and maintenance shall be provided  drainage a natural drainage courses as well as tidal marsh saltwater wetlands under the control of the state of south carolina shall be incorporated into rightsofway b stormwater management features that discharge into or otherwise utilize freshwater wetlands in stormwater management plans shall be incorporated into a drainage easement if they are not incorporated into a natural drainage course rightofway c all artificial drainage improvements shall be incorporated into easements or rightsofway adequate in width and condition to accommodate the improvements and allow for access for maintenance d drainage easements shall be centered along lot boundaries where practical drainage easements may be located in required yards encroachment of drainage easements into building envelopes shall be minimized to the greatest extent practical  water and sewer a water and sewer improvements shall be generally located in rightsofway or easements adequate in width and condition to accommodate the improvements and allow for access for maintenance improvements proposed for dedication to public utilities shall meet or exceed the standards thereof b easements for water and sewer improvements shall be centered along lot boundaries where practical such easements may be located in required yards encroachment of water and sewer easements into building envelopes shall be minimized to the greatest extent practical  other utilities a utilities not specified above including but not limited to telephone electricity and television shall be located in rightsofway or easements adequate in width and condition to accommodate the improvements and allow for access for maintenance b easements shall collocate where practical to minimize encroachment into building envelopes and natural resources 518  adequate oversized and offsite improvements a improvements shall be designed and constructed to serve all current and future phases of the major land development and the planned development district as applicable b oversized improvements the planning commission may require the developer to install capital improvements adequate in size and capacity to serve future development on nearby land where the service provider determines that such improvements are needed to adequately serve future development in the vicinity of the proposed development 1 oversized improvements required during development review the developer shall be notified of the need for oversized improvements prior to approval of the preliminary land development plan and the requirement shall not delay the development review timeline the service provider city of hanahan berkeley county or other shall verify the need for oversized improvements and shall commit to accepting and maintaining the improvements upon completion 2 infrastructure system connectivity road stubs and other improvements designed to ensure interconnected systems of infrastructure in hanahan shall not be considered oversized improvements and shall be considered basic requirements for proposed improvements 3 cost sharing the developer shall be responsible only for costs associated with improvements needed to serve his development including future phases and the planned development district the developer shall install oversized improvements required by the planning commission the service provider shall provide the materials and reimburse the developer for expenses incurred the service provider and the developer may enter into a voluntary alternative arrangement achieving the goal of complete systems of infrastructure c offsite improvements the developer shall be responsible for all capital improvements to existing systems of infrastructure to which the development proposes to connect 1 the developer shall perform any studies needed eg traffic study to determine what improvements to systems will be necessitated by the proposed development the study may be reviewed or performed by the service provider if it accepts the responsibility or an independent third party qualified to review or perform the study 2 the developer shall fully implement improvements that the study concludes are necessitated by the proposed development 3 the planning commission may require that offsite improvements also be oversized to serve future development outside the proposed land development or planned development district in which case oversized improvements standards above shall apply d limitations on city requirements 1 the city of hanahan shall not require a developer to rectify preexisting inadequate levels of service that are unrelated to or out of scale and proportion with the proposed land development and expected impacts thereof the developer shall only be responsible to offset impacts reasonably expected from his proposal at buildout 2 the developer shall not be required to fund or provide equipment maintenance personnel or other operating costs for public infrastructure or
